## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population size P, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. The relationship likely involves density-dependent regulation and possibly time-varying environmental factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (Gompertz-type density dependence, log-based regulation)
- Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Strong Allee cubic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (P + c2) (bistable population dynamics)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (carrying capacity changing with time)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (periodic environmental variation)
- Exponential harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) + c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting/immigration)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**(c2)) (flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Time-dependent rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) + c2 * P (rational density dependence)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (general polynomial regulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation appears as polynomial terms in P: linear P for exponential, quadratic P² for logistic, cubic P³ for Allee effects
- Carrying capacity K manifests as a root of dP/dt when expressed as a polynomial in P — look for factored forms with (K - P) or equivalently (1 + c*P)
- Allee effects (minimum viable population) produce an additional root at small P, creating cubic or higher-order terms in P
- Time-dependent parameters often appear as multiplicative modulation of the intrinsic growth rate: r(t) * f(P)
- Periodic/seasonal forcing appears as sinusoidal multiplication on the growth rate term, modulating carrying capacity or intrinsic rate
- Immigration or harvesting terms appear as additive constants independent of P, shifting equilibria
- Gompertz-type regulation uses log(P) instead of polynomial P, giving different curvature near carrying capacity
- Ratio-dependent terms like P/(1+c*P) indicate resource competition with handling time or interference
- If dP/dt depends explicitly on t (not just through P), the system is non-autonomous, suggesting environmental forcing or regime change
- Bistability in population dynamics corresponds to dP/dt having three real roots in P (two stable equilibria separated by an unstable one)
